Right and wrong are not fixed terms.
What was wrong 50 years ago is right and proper
to-day, and vice versa. Public opinion continually
readjusts her standards of comparison.
“The French nobility of a hundred years
ago,” remarked Carlyle, “said they could afford
to laugh at theories. Then came a man who wrote
a book called ‘The Social Contract.’ The man
was called Jean Jacques Rousseau, and his book
was a theory, and nothing but a theory. The
nobles could laugh at his theory, but their skins
went to bind the second edition of his book,”
W. C. Ranson, an old Herberton (N.Q.)
miner, now in Mashonaland, Africa, writes to the
Wild River Times from the Hartley Hills, 120
miles south of the Zambesi River : —“ Advise the
mining community not to come to this country.
The gold is not worth it, and the fever is a perfect
terror.” He also gives local prices current as
being :—Flour, 2s. 6d, per lb.; sugar, 5s. per lb. ;
tea, 10s. per lb. ; boots, 32s. a-pair; donkeys, £15
each ; horses, from £80 to £95 each. The rivers
are infested with crocodiles and hippopotami ;
the country abounds in lions, wolves, buffaloes,
wild pigs, ostriches, &c.
Kate Elizabeth Day, summoned in London
for neglecting her three little girls, the eldest
5 years and 10 months old, deposed that she had
been deserted by her husband and had since got
her living as a paper-bag maker. “ I am paid 4|d.
per 1000 for it, and have to find my own paste.”
She had had no work for a fortnight. The prose-
cuting officer asked the woman if she would give
up the children to his society. “No,” she replied,
“I love my children.” The magistrate advised
her to do her best, and decided to adjourn the
case for a month. The defendant took her chil-
dren and went away from the court crying, “ to do
her best!”
Pat. Perkins, the Queensland Jonah, and
the pig-headed opponent of Labour in the Queens-
land Parliament, is the son of a Tipperary
labourer. Pat. made his money out of the Vic-
torian mines, baffled the efforts of a few sea-cap-
tains to wreck him, took to brewing, made his
way into the Assembly on a flood of beer, and got
the post of Minister for Lands from MTlwraith.
At a general election some years back Pat. got
more votes than the number on the roll of his con-
stituency. He now hob-nobs with the Guv’nah.
Much money, many friends. If there is a
man who realises this it is Morris Collmann, of
Bendigo, one time a proprietor of the well-known
Collmann and Tacchi Mine, near Eaglehawk.
Then Morris could writ& his cheque for close on
six figures and have it honoured, too. He was
affectionately regarded by the miners, for was it
not he who said that men should, in his mine,
work no more than eight hours underground ? Ho
left for Germany years ago, and with a partner
entered into corn-speculation, after prudently
banking £10,000 in his own behalf “ against a
rainy day.” The firm’s speculations proved
disastrous ; every cent embarked in the business
was lost, and Morris discovered that his partner’s
actions had rendered him liable also for the
£10,000 ; so once more ho returned to Australia in
the hopes of retrieving his fortunes. On his
return his wealthy friends knew him not; but his
poorer ones, the miners, have not forgotten him.
There is a small stipend attached to the Mining
Board membership, and the miners, grateful for
Colhnann’s actions in the past, always return him
at the head of the poll. He is old now, and not
capable of the work he once could do.
Bathurst (N.S.W.) Advocate rises to
poetic yearnings on the subject of the small
infants who planted trees on Arbor Day, and
soars on the wings of the morning over the bright
land of song. This is the hunk ; —
And the best wish we can publish for the benefit of that
generation is that they may grow up from saplings to be
sturdy, upright men and women, with hearts brave as
oaks, ideas lofty as pines, minds fragrant as cedars, and
virtues manifold as the leaves through which CEolus
breathes his melodies. May their lives be as pure as the
lily, noble as the rose, sweet as the violet, lovable as the
forget-me-not, and yet humble as the daisy—the poets’
flower—the emblem of simplicity.
Also, may they be as enduring as the kitchen-
stove, and strong like the butter in our hash-
tower, and vigorous like Parkes’ I.O.U.’s, and
as swift as Dan. O’Connor rushing to welcome an
eminent visitor or to get out of the road of a dead
failure, or as the wild inroad of the Australian
gentry surging into the refreshment-room at
Gov’ment ’Ouse. The Advocate likewise con-
siders that a Minister of Education is no good
unless he possesses the “ rare exotic of ideality.’

The eminent Scottish J udge, Lord Presi-
dent luglis, whoso death was recently cabled,
defended Madeleine Smith, accused of murdering
by poison her lover, Emile L’Angelier, a genera-
tion ago. The prosecution, it may be remem-
bered, depended entirely on circumstantial evi-
dence, and it was to the danger of depending ex-
clusively upon testimony of that nature that lie
addressed himself in his peroration—which, re-
garded by competent critics as the most impres-
sive ever delivered in a British Court, secured the
acquittal of the accused. Inglis said :
I fear that this is no solitary case. The recollection or
the reading of any of us may recall occasions
When, after execution, judgment hath
Repented o’er her doom.
To rely upon your reason only is nothing less than im-
piously to refuse to call to your aid, in the performance
of a momentous duty, the noblest gifts that God has im-
planted in your breasts'. To determine guilt or
innocence by the light of intellect alone is the exclusive
prerogative of infallibility, and when man’s presumptuous
arrogance tempts him to usurp the attribute of Om-
niscience, he only exposes the weakness and frailty of bis
nature. Then, indeed,
Man, proud man
1 tressed in a little brief authority,
Most ignorant,of what he’s most assured,
Plays such fantastic tricks before high Heaven
As make the angels weep.

The captain of the Glenelg (S.A.)Fir 0
Brigade holds the belt for pure cussedness. II s
was called to a fire, and when he arrived there
found that the burning house was outside his
district boundary. He returned with his reel and
telephoned to Adelaide for permission to put out
the fire. When he returned the house was burned
down.

Bishop Butt (R.C.), of England, has been
praying for fine weather that the English harvest
may be saved. Bishop Butt (who seeks, for tin-
pot human purposes, to interfere with arrange-
ments made at the beginning of all time) might
just as well stand in a big butcher’s basket and
pray to the Lord to send him strength enough to
lift himself by the handle.
Dear Bulletin,— Sir Alfred Stephen’s
first contribution to the Australian press was over
the nom-de-plume of “Common Sense,” and ap-
peared in the Hobart Town Gazette of 1824.
His latest contribution was the skilful bit of
special pleading which was published (in “ leaded”
type) by the S.M. Herald on 24th Sept, over the
signature of “Nostri Juris.” Every newspaper
article penned by Sir Alfred can be identified by
style, apart from any other datum of “internal
evidence,” which always sticks out a furlong from
his contributions. Curiously enough, the “Com-
mon Sense ” article was suggested by a question
of jurisdiction and the necessity of bolstering up
the judicial powers that were. So was the “Nostri
Juris” screed, and the motto which headed the
former : “I know my Q. without a prompter ”
might, with equal appropriateness, have intro-
duced the latter.— Price Warung.

In the Transvaal, the members of either
House receive £3 per diem while the Houses are
in session. The President gets a salary of £8o(lU
a year. He lives very quietly—never entertains;
indeed, he never gives a bite or sup to a soul.
He is reported to have amassed a large fortune.

J. O. Wascoe, who kept the little inn on
Lapstouo HH1 long ere the railway crossed the
N.S.W. Blue Mountains, is dead. When the
iron horse got up the Zig-zag “ Wascoe was the
iirst station opened, but the name has been since
changed to “ Blaxland ’’-after the old-time
explorer. Wascoe was 73 years of age and a
nephew of the distinguished Indian General, bir
James Outran).
Bishop Tucker, of Maoriland, reportsthat
in Uganda (Africa) a man will readily do three
mouths’ work for a Testament. Now any, man
might say he would do three months work for a
Testament, but no one could know that he would
really do it save by actual experiment. Evi.
dently. therefore, some gospel-grinder does try
the experiment, and The Bulletin hereby
records its conviction that the expounder who
would thus trade on the ignorance of the sweated
heathen is a loathsome swindler, a base sneak-
thief, and the worst variety of mercenary
hypocrite. Strangely enough, Bishop Tucker
doesn’t seem to have denounced the low-grade
pirate who thus got three months’ work out of the
illiterate African by scaring him with stories
about Gehenna, and what gaol he is now in for
false pretences wasn’t even mentioned.
At the Depths of the Mine.
(FOR THE BULLETIN.)
At the depths with the animate world throbbing
o’er you in life and decay—
In the wry wrought cells where the curled dank
mists round the weak lights play —
You are hid from the rays of the sun through
aeons and aeons untold,
Ah, see what the ages have d.ne, with the force
that is new and is old !
That infinite force rebuilds, destroys—remcdels
anew,
In the light of the stars it fulfills ; in the darkness
invaded by you.
Down ’mid the works of time,
That the ages built sublime —
Built in the light of the past,
With the sun raying down to their deeps,
Base upon base in the vast
Sphered mould of the planet’s cast,
In the heart of the great earth sleeps !
Where the sunlight hath lived and ended, full
glad iii its passionate day,
The light of the toiler is blended one moment, O
Earth, in thine aye ;
For what are the days or the years when the
kindled small flame shall be dead ?
And the steel-hurling arm that appears with its
fire that empowers shall be shed.
But for you, O toiler, who pierce the great living
breast of the earth,
There is time to bo sad in the fierce beast-moil
that is thine from thy birth !
Down ’mid the works of time,
That the ages built sublime —
Built in the light of the past.
With the sun raying down to their deeps,
Base upon base in the vast
Sphered mffuld of the planet’s cast,
In the heart of the great earth sleeps !
HERBERT YOUNG.
W ollongong.
